Obama's health care law</a>.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>\"This is the time we\u2019re going to get it done,\" Trump told a group of House Republican committee chairs who gathered at the White House to plan strategy for their effort to repeal and replace the Affordable Care Act. \"I think it\u2019s just something that\u2019s going to happen very shortly.\"</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Trump suggested that the architects of the 2010 Obamacare law knew it would collapse in 2017 because Obama would no longer be in office, and his "http://rssfeeds.usatoday.com/~/279385860/0/usatoday-newstopstories~Trump-predicts-passage-of-GOP-health-care-bill/", "date": "03-10-2017", "source": "new-york-times", "text": "CLOSE Skip in Skip x Embed x Share President Donald Trump met with the House chairmen and women whose committees are aiding the drive to repeal and replace the Affordable Care Act. Sounding a familiar theme, Trump said action is needed 'now' to prevent an 'Obamcare disaster.' (March 10) AP\n\nPresident Trump speaks during a meeting on health care March 10. (Photo: Evan Vucci, AP)\n\nWASHINGTON \u2014 Despite opposition from some conservatives, President Trump on Friday predicted fairly rapid approval of a replacement to President Obama's health care law.\n\n\"This is the time we\u2019re going to get it done,\" Trump told a group of House Republican committee chairs who gathered at the White House to plan strategy for their effort to repeal and replace the Affordable Care Act. \"I think it\u2019s just something that\u2019s going to happen very shortly.\"\n\nTrump suggested that the architects of the 2010 Obamacare law knew it would collapse in 2017 because Obama would no longer be in office, and his successor would have to deal with the fallout.\n\nTrump has talked with congressional Republicans throughout the week, in part to address conservative criticism of a plan rolled out by the House GOP leadership.\n\nRead more:\n\nOne Republican who did not attend the White House gathering \u2014 Rep. Mark Meadows, R-N.C., chairman of the conservative group known as the House Freedom Caucus \u2014 said the plan would make it easier for young healthy people to opt out of insurance markets, raising costs for everyone else.\n\n\"Obviously, we're going to try to make this bill better where it actually lowers premiums,\" Meadows said. \"That's why there's not enough votes, because at this point, the No. 1 priority \u2014 the top priority, you can throw everything away \u2014 is driving premiums down. If we don't do that, we will have failed, and we must do that in order to be successful.\"\n\nIn a series of interviews, House Speaker Paul Ryan, R-Wis., and other backers of the bill said it would lower costs by reducing government regulations and creating more choices for insurance purchasers.\n\n\"We should have a free market in health care, a patient-centered system run by consumers,\" Ryan told radio host Hugh Hewitt. \"That\u2019s why we have risk pools, tax credits and health savings accounts.\"\n\nHouse Speaker Paul Ryan uses charts and graphs to make his case for the GOP's long-awaited plan to repeal and replace the Affordable Care Act on March 9. (Photo: J. Scott Applewhite, AP)\n\nTrump, Ryan and other backers of the House health care plan said provisions will be added in three phases and many of the conservative complaints will be addressed in phases two and three.\n\nDemocrats said Republicans' plans to eliminate subsidies and fines on people who do not buy health insurance will increase costs for millions, rendering them unable to afford insurance.\n\nRep. Diana DeGette, D-Colo., said Democrats will try to block an Obamacare repeal because \"we\u2019re not about to let the tyranny of the majority in Congress leave people vulnerable just because Republicans want to jam through an ill-conceived bill.\"\n\nThe Republicans who met with Trump on Friday called the session a good one, and they downplayed GOP divisions over health care.\n\nRep. Kevin Brady, R-Texas, chairman of the House Ways and Means Committee, said, \"There is so much more that unites Republicans than divides Republicans on this issue.\"\n\nRead more:\n\nRead or Share
